In 1204 the Body of St. Lucy is brought to the Island (S. Giorgio
Maggiore), then transferred to the church of the Annunciation (now at
Church of St. Jeremiah)

Patriarch of Constantinople Giovanni Contarini, a guest of the
Monastery, later buried at S. Giorgio Maggiore

personne related

- San Severino Bishop (sixth century), venerated in the crypt, in the
  ancient cathedral, the Castle.

- San Vittorino, his brother, venerated in the collegiate church of
  Pioraco.

San Domenico Loricato (Dominicus Loricatus, X century), whose body is
venerated in the church of St. Anne in front, under the main altar, the
bones of the saint contained within a wooden statue of Bigioli, feast on
14 October.

  - Santa Filomena, Sant\'Ippolito soldier and martyr, St. Justin priest and
    martyr; the body of the saint and the relics of the martyrs, are
    venerated in the Basilica of San Lorenzo in Doliolo.

  - Blessed Pellegrino from Falerone (m. 1233) and Bentivoglio De Bonis (m.
    1232), Franciscan, venerated in the Shrine of Our Lady of the Lights,
    run by the Cistercians, where rests their bodies.

Sant\'Illuminato monaco (XIII century), venerated in a beautiful urn,
finely chiseled, in the monastery of the Cistercians where he is buried.
Festival May 11.

  - Blessed Pupelli Marseilles (d. 1298), Tertiary of St. Augustine, buried
    in the church of Sant\'Agostino.

Bartholomew of San Severino of Brand (m. 1390), the Kingdom of Naples
commander created The Viceroy of Abruzzo by King Charles III.

Santa Margherita di Cesolo, called The Barefoot, († 1395), celebrated on
5 August. Body in veneration in the homonymous village church.

The brothers Lorenzo (about 1374 - before 1420) and Jacopo Salimbeni
(? - After 1427), painters.

  - Blessed Camilla Gentiles, Martyr all\'Uvaiolo in 1486, remains behind
    the main altar of the church of San Domenico. His feast on July 27.

Dominic, a Franciscan, born in Patrignolo in the first half of the
fifteenth century, lived, died and buried in Leonessa April 20, 1497,
where he is venerated.

Ludovico Urbani (active in the second half of the fifteenth century),
painter.

Lorenzo d\'Alessandro (1445 - 1501), painter.

Domenico Indivini (1445? -1502), Carver and engraver, author of the
choir of the Upper Basilica of Assisi. He began a carving school that
went with his brother Nicholas and with Acciaccaferri family.

Ludovico Lazzarelli (February 4, 1447 - June 23, 1500), Italian poet and
philosopher of the early Renaissance.

  - Blessed Peter Macaroni, Franciscan, born in San Severino Marche in the
    early decades of the fifteenth century, lived and buried September 23,
    1507 in the convent of Santa Maria delle Grazie, now the Sanctuary of
    San Pacifico.

  - Blessed Marchesina Luzi (m. 1510), Tertiary of St. Augustine, buried in
    the church of Sant'Agostino.

Angelo Massarelli, Secretary of the Council of Trent.

Antonio Giacomo Acciaccaferri (XVI century), painter.

Bartolomeo Eustachi better known as Bartolomeo Eustachio (1500 or
1514-1574), anatomist and discoverer of the Eustachian tubes. Buried in
the mentioned church of San Domenico.

Francesca Trigli servant of God, according to the Serrone, (1557 -
1601), Franciscan tertiary, venerated at the shrine of Our Lady of the
Lights, run by the Cistercians, where his body rests.

  - Antonio Talpa (1536-1624), religious.

  - Servant of God Lorenza Mantovani, died March 28, 1663, buried in the
    church Cagnore.

San Pacific Divine, a Franciscan (1653 - 1721), revered by many
devotees, even strangers, in the homonymous local shrine, (officiated by
the friars of the same order), where his body rests. Feast on September
24, if working, the following Sunday.

Lost or likely lost graves:

  - Bl. Pietro da Treja, monk, 2/20

[^1]: Blesseds buried here: **Friar Angel (+1258); Friar Leo (+1271) -
who was St. Francis' confessor; Friar Masseo of Merignano (+1280);
Friar Rufino (+1249) -St. Agnes and St. Clare's cousin; Friar
William of England**

[^2]: Possibly at their Rome house? It's located at Clivo di Monte del
Gallo, 27, near the Vatican.

[^3]: In memory of Felice of Barbarano. Her memorial reads, "In memory
of Felicia of Barborono: The virginity, piety, humility, patience
and other Christian virtues that distinguished her and made her well
enough known in her time was followed by oblivion in this sacred
temple where she rests in the tomb. \[Her virtues\] have been
vindicated by this memorial, placed in the year of salvation 1674 so
that all may mourn \[the loss of this\] splendid example of
holiness, \[she who\] died 20 April 1553."
